Thought for 1m 1s
Summary
This guide applies a four-phase migration strategy to isolate and modernize the util.Resources helper from the JBoss kitchensink application into a standalone Spring Boot 3.x (Java 21) service that runs locally alongside the legacy system .

Phased Extraction Approach
Phase 1: Identify and Isolate the Module
Locate the helper class. In the kitchensink codebase, find org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util.Resources to serve as our extraction target .

Extract into its own Maven module. Create a new module (e.g., kitchensink-util) within the same multi-module Maven project, copying Resources.java and preserving its package path .

Phase 2: Bootstrap a Spring Boot Skeleton
Generate via Spring Initializr. Open https://start.spring.io, choose Maven, Java, Spring Boot 3.x, and Java 21 .

Set project metadata. Use Group com.example.kitchensink, Artifact util-resources, Package com.example.kitchensink.util .

Add dependencies. In the Dependencies box, select Spring Web, Spring Data JPA, and H2 Database .

Import into IntelliJ. Unzip the project archive and import it as a Maven project in IntelliJ IDEA .

Ensure Java 21 and Boot 3.x. If the generated POM defaults to an older version, update the <java.version> to 21 and the parent BOM‚Äôs <version> to your chosen Spring Boot 3.x release .

Phase 3: Migrate Code into the New Service
Copy the class. Move Resources.java into src/main/java/com/example/kitchensink/util/Resources.java in the new module.

Update package imports. Replace all javax.* imports with jakarta.* per Jakarta EE 9 requirements in Spring Boot 3.x .

Annotate for Spring. Add @Component (or @Service) to Resources and any necessary @PostConstruct or @Autowired annotations to wire dependencies .

Create the bootstrap class. In the same package, add:

@SpringBootApplication
public class Application {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SpringApplication.run(Application.class, args);
    }
}
``` .
Phase 4: Run and Validate Locally
Configure H2 in application.properties:

spring.datasource.url=jdbc:h2:mem:testdb
spring.datasource.driverClassName=org.h2.Driver
spring.datasource.username=sa
spring.datasource.password=
spring.h2.console.enabled=true
(Spring Boot auto-configures an in-memory H2 by default)
Baeldung
.

Launch the service. In IntelliJ, right-click Application.java ‚Üí Run, or execute ./mvnw spring-boot:run at the module root .

Verify endpoints. Access http://localhost:8080 (and /h2-console at port 8080) to confirm the Resources component is active alongside the legacy kitchensink on its original port.

Following these steps, you‚Äôll have a minimal, Java 21 Spring Boot 3.x service for Resources running locally, while the rest of kitchensink remains on JBoss‚Äîenabling incremental migration with minimal risk.

JetBrains

JetBrains

The error you‚Äôre seeing is because the kitchensink POM you opened still refers to a parent POM that lives one level up in the jboss-eap-quickstarts repo‚Äîwhich you don‚Äôt have in your project right now. IntelliJ can‚Äôt find it, so it won‚Äôt fully import the Maven project.

You have two easy options:

Option A: Work in the full Quickstarts repo (recommended)
Clone the entire quickstarts (so you get the parent POM):

cd ~/Developer/java-samples
git clone --branch 8.0.x https://github.com/jboss-developer/jboss-eap-quickstarts.git
Open IntelliJ ‚Üí Open ‚Üí select the freshly-cloned jboss-eap-quickstarts folder (the one containing the top-level pom.xml).

Let IntelliJ import that as a Maven project (it will now find the parent).

In the Maven tool window you‚Äôll see modules like kitchensink, transaction, etc.

You can now right-click the root node and do New ‚Üí Module ‚Üí Maven to create kitchensink-util as we outlined.

Option B: Make kitchensink standalone
If you really only want kitchensink and your new util module:

Move your kitchensink folder out of the quickstarts tree (so you aren‚Äôt missing its parent).

In that folder create a new parent POM (pom.xml) alongside the existing one:

<project xmlns="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0"
         xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
         xsi:schemaLocation="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
                             http://maven.apache.org/xsd/maven-4.0.0.xsd">
  <modelVersion>4.0.0</modelVersion>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-parent</artifactId>
  <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
  <packaging>pom</packaging>
  <modules>
    <module>kitchensink</module>
    <module>kitchensink-util</module>
  </modules>
</project>
Edit kitchensink/pom.xml:

Remove its <parent> block entirely.

Change its <groupId> to com.example.kitchensink.

Open that new parent folder in IntelliJ (it will now import a two-module project).

Follow the same New ‚Üí Module ‚Üí Maven flow to add kitchensink-util.

I recommend Option A (just clone the full quickstarts)‚Äîthat way you don‚Äôt have to hand-edit POMs, and IntelliJ will import smoothly. Let me know which you‚Äôd like to proceed with, and then we‚Äôll continue with copying over Resources.java.

Re-import the POM as a Maven project

.

JetBrains IntelliJ Support
.

Watch out for spaces in your path
IntelliJ (especially over WSL) can fail to resolve files when your project or module folder name contains spaces. Renaming directories to remove spaces often cures ‚Äúunable to locate‚Äù issues
YouTrack

Invalidate caches and restart
If files are still ‚Äúghosted,‚Äù try File ‚Üí Invalidate Caches / Restart‚Ä¶ to clear any stale indexing that might be pointing at old paths

You‚Äôre seeing ‚ÄúUnlink Maven Projects‚Äù because IntelliJ thinks the POM is already part of a Maven build‚Äîbut it can‚Äôt resolve its parent, so it‚Äôs broken. The quickest way to fix this (without pulling in the entire quickstarts repository) is to make kitchensink a standalone Maven project:

1. Remove the bad parent declaration
Open kitchensink/pom.xml in the editor.

Find and delete this entire block:

<parent>
  <groupId>org.jboss.eap.quickstarts</groupId>
  <artifactId>jboss-eap-quickstart-parent</artifactId>
  <version>6.0.0.redhat-00001</version>
  <relativePath/>
</parent>
Directly under <project> add your own coordinates, for example:

<groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
<artifactId>kitchensink</artifactId>
<version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
<packaging>war</packaging>
(You can keep the original <name> and <description> if you like.)

2. Reload the Maven project in IntelliJ
In the Maven tool window (the ‚ÄúM‚Äù pane on the right), click the Refresh icon (or right-click the kitchensink entry ‚Üí Maven ‚Üí Reload Project).

If you still see errors, right-click the root pom.xml ‚Üí Maven ‚Üí Sync Project.

You should now have a clean, standalone Maven module (no more ‚Äúunable to locate parent‚Äù errors). The little ‚ÄúM‚Äù badge on the kitchensink folder will remain, but the build will succeed.

Once that‚Äôs green, you can proceed with Phase 1B exactly as before:

Right-click the root node ‚Üí New ‚Üí Module‚Ä¶ ‚Üí Maven, etc.

Create kitchensink-util and copy over Resources.java.

Let me know when your kitchensink POM builds cleanly, and we‚Äôll extract the helper class!

Thought for 13 seconds
Those red warnings are just Maven telling you it can‚Äôt find the JBoss Quickstarts parent POM‚Äôs repositories (we removed the parent that declared them). You have two choices:

1. Ignore them for now
You don‚Äôt need to compile the entire legacy kitchensink module‚Äîonly our new kitchensink-util module. As long as Maven sees the module (the ‚ÄúM‚Äù badge) and can compile util, you can safely carry on.

2. Restore the JBoss repository definitions
If you do want the legacy module to build cleanly, add this to your root pom.xml (just under the <project> element):

<repositories>
  <repository>
    <id>jboss-public</id>
    <name>JBoss Public Repository Group</name>
    <url>https://repository.jboss.org/nexus/content/groups/public/</url>
    <layout>default</layout>
  </repository>
</repositories>
<pluginRepositories>
  <pluginRepository>
    <id>jboss-public</id>
    <url>https://repository.jboss.org/nexus/content/groups/public/</url>
  </pluginRepository>
</pluginRepositories>

<project xmlns="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0" xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
         xsi:schemaLocation="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0 http://maven.apache.org/maven-v4_0_0.xsd">
    <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
    <artifactId>kitchensink</artifactId>
    <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
    <packaging>war</packaging>
    <modelVersion>4.0.0</modelVersion>
    <name>Quickstart: kitchensink</name>
    <description>A starter Jakarta EE web application project for use in JBoss EAP</description>

    <licenses>
        <license>
            <name>Apache License, Version 2.0</name>
            <url>http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0.html</url>
            <distribution>repo</distribution>
        </license>
    </licenses>

    <properties>
        <!-- The versions for BOMs, Dependencies and Plugins -->
        <version.server.bom>8.0.0.GA-redhat-00009</version.server.bom>
        <version.eap.maven.plugin>1.0.0.Final-redhat-00014</version.eap.maven.plugin>
    </properties>

    <repositories>
        <!-- keep this repository the first -->
        <repository>
            <id>jboss-public-maven-repository</id>
            <name>JBoss Public Maven Repository</name>
            <url>https://repository.jboss.org/nexus/content/groups/public/</url>
            <releases>
                <enabled>true</enabled>
                <updatePolicy>never</updatePolicy>
            </releases>
            <snapshots>
                <enabled>true</enabled>
                <updatePolicy>never</updatePolicy>

You‚Äôre almost there‚Äîbut right now you‚Äôve got a single ‚Äúkitchensink‚Äù module with no parent to tie in your new kitchensink-util module. Let‚Äôs quickly reshape your Phase-1 folder into a two‚Äìmodule Maven project:

1. Lift out a Parent POM
Go up one level from kitchensink/ (into your phase1/ folder).

Create a new file named pom.xml alongside the existing kitchensink directory.

Put this into it:

<project xmlns="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0"
         xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
         xsi:schemaLocation="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
                             http://maven.apache.org/xsd/maven-4.0.0.xsd">
  <modelVersion>4.0.0</modelVersion>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-parent</artifactId>
  <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
  <packaging>pom</packaging>

  <modules>
    <module>kitchensink</module>
    <module>kitchensink-util</module>
  </modules>
</project>
Move your existing kitchensink/pom.xml (the one you posted) into that same kitchensink/ folder (it‚Äôs already there), but remove from it the <groupId>, <version>, and <packaging> lines‚Äîyou‚Äôll inherit those from the parent. At minimum, make sure it now looks like:

<parent>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-parent</artifactId>
  <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
</parent>
<artifactId>kitchensink</artifactId>
<packaging>war</packaging>
(All other dependencies, repositories, profiles stay as-is.)

Reload in IntelliJ: open the Maven tool window and hit Refresh. You should now see two modules, kitchensink and kitchensink-util (the latter will be empty for now).

2. Create kitchensink-util
Right-click the new parent node in Project ‚Üí New ‚Üí Module‚Ä¶

Select Maven, click Next, and fill in:

GroupId: com.example.kitchensink

ArtifactId: kitchensink-util

Version: 1.0-SNAPSHOT

Packaging: jar

Finish ‚Üí IntelliJ will add <module>kitchensink-util</module> to the parent POM (you‚Äôll see it in the parent‚Äôs <modules>).

3. Copy Resources.java
Expand kitchensink/src/main/java/org/jboss/as/quickstarts/kitchensink/util/Resources.java.

Right-click ‚Üí Copy.

Under kitchensink-util/src/main/java right-click ‚Üí New ‚Üí Package and enter org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util.

Right-click that package ‚Üí Paste ‚Üí confirm.

4. Verify
In the Maven tool window you should now have two buildable modules.

If it builds with no errors, you‚Äôve successfully completed Phase 1!

Let me know as soon as your two-module project compiles cleanly, and we‚Äôll move on to bootstrapping Spring Boot in kitchensink-util.

Let‚Äôs straighten out your folder layout so Maven/IntelliJ can see a true ‚Äúmulti-module‚Äù project under a common parent POM. Right now you have:

kitchensink-modern/

We need to:

From Finder or terminal:

cd ~/Developer/java-samples/kitchensink-modern/v1
mv "2 phase1" phase1
Now your tree is:

kitchensink-modern/v1/phase1/
‚îî‚îÄ kitchensink/    ‚Üê your existing legacy module
2. Create the parent POM

<project xmlns="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0"
         xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
         xsi:schemaLocation="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0

  <packaging>pom</packaging>

  <modules>

    <module>kitchensink-util</module>
  </modules>
</project>
3. Adjust the existing child POM
Open phase1/kitchensink/pom.xml and:

Remove its <groupId>, <version>, and <packaging> elements.

Add a <parent> block at the top, immediately below <project>:

<parent>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-parent</artifactId>
  <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
</parent>
<artifactId>kitchensink</artifactId>
<packaging>war</packaging>
Keep all the rest of its <dependencies>, <repositories>, <profiles>, etc.

4. Re-open (or refresh) in IntelliJ
In IntelliJ, File ‚Üí Open‚Ä¶, choose the phase1/ folder (the one now containing your new pom.xml and the kitchensink/ subfolder).

kitchensink

kitchensink-util (gray, not yet created)

5. Create kitchensink-util

Right-click the phase1 root in Project view ‚Üí New ‚Üí Module‚Ä¶

Select Maven, click Next.

Fill in:

GroupId: com.example.kitchensink

ArtifactId: kitchensink-util

Version: 1.0-SNAPSHOT

Packaging: jar

Click Finish. IntelliJ will add <module>kitchensink-util</module> to your parent POM automatically.

Under phase1/kitchensink-util/src/main/java, right-click ‚Üí New ‚Üí Package ‚Üí enter
org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util

Right-click that package ‚Üí Paste ‚Üí confirm.

You should see BUILD SUCCESS.

Congrats! You now have:

A parent project (kitchensink-parent)

Two child modules (kitchensink legacy WAR and kitchensink-util JAR)

Ready for Phase 2: bootstrapping Spring Boot in kitchensink-util.

That error isn‚Äôt about the package name itself‚Äîit‚Äôs IntelliJ telling you that this directory isn‚Äôt yet a Java ‚Äúsource root,‚Äù so it won‚Äôt let you create packages under it. Here‚Äôs how to fix:

Mark src/main/java as a Source Root

In the Project tool window, switch to the plain Project view (use the dropdown at the top of that pane).

Expand to kitchensink-util/src/main.

Right-click the java folder ‚Üí Mark Directory as ‚Üí Sources Root.

You should see that folder turn blue or get a little ‚ÄúSources‚Äù tag.

Create the Package

Now right-click that java folder (or inside it) ‚Üí New ‚Üí Package.

Enter org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util and hit Enter.

IntelliJ will create the directory structure and allow you to add classes.

Paste Resources.java

Expand your legacy module‚Äôs util package, copy Resources.java, then paste into this newly-created package in kitchensink-util.

Rebuild

In the Maven tool window, under kitchensink-util ‚Üí Lifecycle, double-click compile.

You should now get BUILD SUCCESS.

That gets kitchensink-util properly set up with src/main/java as a source root so you can proceed with Phase 2.

Your new util module is missing the Jakarta EE APIs it relies on (CDI and JPA). Let‚Äôs add those to its pom.xml so it can compile:

Open kitchensink-util/pom.xml.

<!-- CDI API (includes jakarta.enterprise.inject and spi packages) -->
<dependency>
  <groupId>jakarta.enterprise</groupId>
  <artifactId>jakarta.enterprise.cdi-api</artifactId>
  <version>4.0.1</version>
  <scope>provided</scope>
</dependency>

<!-- JPA API (for jakarta.persistence) -->
<dependency>
  <groupId>jakarta.persistence</groupId>
  <artifactId>jakarta.persistence-api</artifactId>
  <version>3.1.0</version>
  <scope>provided</scope>
</dependency>
You can adjust versions to match your Jakarta EE BOM if you import one later; these are the current GA releases.

Save the POM.

In the Maven tool window, Refresh (üîÑ), then under kitchensink-util ‚Üí Lifecycle double-click compile.

Great‚Äîyour kitchensink-util module is now compiling cleanly on Java 21. You‚Äôll notice the warning recommending --release 21; we‚Äôll address that when polishing, but let‚Äôs move on to Phase 2: turning this helper module into a minimal Spring Boot 3.x service.

Phase 2: Bootstrap a Spring Boot Skeleton in kitchensink-util
1. Convert to a Spring Boot project
Open kitchensink-util/pom.xml.

Add the Spring Boot parent and plugin management just below your <modelVersion>:

<parent>
  <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
  <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-parent</artifactId>
  <version>3.2.8</version>
  <relativePath/>  <!-- lookup parent from Maven Central -->
</parent>
Under your existing <properties>, add:

<java.version>21</java.version>
Replace your <dependencies> block with this minimal set (which still provides CDI/JPA if you need them later):

<dependencies>
  <!-- Expose our helper as a Spring bean -->
  <dependency>
    <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
    <artifactId>spring-boot-starter</artifactId>
  </dependency>

  <!-- For REST endpoints later (optional) -->
  <dependency>
    <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
    <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-web</artifactId>
  </dependency>

  <!-- (Retain Jakarta APIs if needed) -->
  <dependency>
    <groupId>jakarta.enterprise</groupId>
    <artifactId>jakarta.enterprise.cdi-api</artifactId>
    <scope>provided</scope>
  </dependency>
  <dependency>
    <groupId>jakarta.persistence</groupId>
    <artifactId>jakarta.persistence-api</artifactId>
    <scope>provided</scope>
  </dependency>
</dependencies>
Add the Spring Boot Maven plugin at the end of your <build> section:

<build>
  <plugins>
    <plugin>
      <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
      <artifactId>spring-boot-maven-plugin</artifactId>
    </plugin>
  </plugins>
</build>
2. Create the Application Entry Point
Under kitchensink-util/src/main/java, navigate to your package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util.

Right-click that package ‚Üí New ‚Üí Java Class ‚Üí name it Application.

Paste in:

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import org.springframework.boot.SpringApplication;
import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.SpringBootApplication;

@SpringBootApplication
public class Application {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SpringApplication.run(Application.class, args);
    }
}
3. Expose the Helper as a Spring Bean
Open your existing Resources.java.

At the top of the class, add:

import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;
Annotate the class:

@Component
public class Resources {
    // ‚Ä¶ existing code ‚Ä¶
}
4. Run Locally
In the Maven tool window, under kitchensink-util ‚Üí Plugins ‚Üí spring-boot ‚Üí spring-boot:run, double-click spring-boot:run.

You should see Spring Boot start up on port 8080.

Hit http://localhost:8080/actuator/health (you‚Äôll need to add the Actuator starter later) or simply confirm the ‚ÄúStarted Application‚Äù banner in the logs.

After these steps you‚Äôll have:

A standalone Spring Boot 3.x (Java 21) service in kitchensink-util.

Your legacy kitchensink WAR still untouched, running wherever you had it on JBoss.

ChatGPT said:
Good catch‚ÄîMaven only allows a single <parent>, so you can‚Äôt both inherit from your kitchensink-parent and Spring Boot‚Äôs starter parent. Instead, keep your kitchensink-parent as the sole parent and import Spring Boot‚Äôs dependency management via a BOM. Here‚Äôs what you need:

<project ‚Ä¶>
  <modelVersion>4.0.0</modelVersion>

  <!-- Keep your parent -->
  <parent>
    <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
    <artifactId>kitchensink-parent</artifactId>
    <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
  </parent>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>

  <properties>
    <java.version>21</java.version>
    <project.build.sourceEncoding>UTF-8</project.build.sourceEncoding>
  </properties>

  <!-- Import the Spring Boot BOM instead of using it as parent -->
  <dependencyManagement>
    <dependencies>
      <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-dependencies</artifactId>
        <version>3.2.8</version>
        <type>pom</type>
        <scope>import</scope>
      </dependency>
    </dependencies>
  </dependencyManagement>

  <dependencies>
    <!-- Spring Boot starters -->
    <dependency>
      <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
      <artifactId>spring-boot-starter</artifactId>
    </dependency>
    <dependency>
      <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
      <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-web</artifactId>
    </dependency>

    <!-- Retain Jakarta APIs as provided -->
    <dependency>
      <groupId>jakarta.enterprise</groupId>
      <artifactId>jakarta.enterprise.cdi-api</artifactId>
      <scope>provided</scope>
    </dependency>
    <dependency>
      <groupId>jakarta.persistence</groupId>
      <artifactId>jakarta.persistence-api</artifactId>
      <scope>provided</scope>
    </dependency>
  </dependencies>

  <build>
    <plugins>
      <!-- Register the Spring Boot Maven plugin -->
      <plugin>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-maven-plugin</artifactId>
      </plugin>
    </plugins>
  </build>
</project>
What you did:

Kept your existing parent so you don‚Äôt break the multi-module setup.

Imported Spring Boot‚Äôs BOM (spring-boot-dependencies) in <dependencyManagement> to get all Spring versions.

Added the two core starters (spring-boot-starter and spring-boot-starter-web).

Registered the spring-boot-maven-plugin under <build> so you can mvn spring-boot:run.

Now hit Refresh in the Maven tool window and then run kitchensink-util ‚Üí Plugins ‚Üí spring-boot:run. You should get a Spring Boot banner on port 8080. Let me know how it goes!

        <project.build.sourceEncoding>UTF-8</project.build.sourceEncoding>

ChatGPT said:
Here‚Äôs the complete, corrected kitchensink-util/pom.xml incorporating your existing parent, importing the Spring Boot BOM, adding the Spring Boot Maven plugin, and defining the starters alongside your Jakarta APIs:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<project xmlns="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0"
         xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
         xsi:schemaLocation="
           http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
           http://maven.apache.org/xsd/maven-4.0.0.xsd">

    <modelVersion>4.0.0</modelVersion>

    <!-- Inherit from your multi-module parent -->
    <parent>
        <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
        <artifactId>kitchensink-parent</artifactId>
        <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
    </parent>

    <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>

    <properties>
        <!-- Use Java 21 -->
        <java.version>21</java.version>
        <project.build.sourceEncoding>UTF-8</project.build.sourceEncoding>
    </properties>

    <!-- Import Spring Boot's dependency management -->
    <dependencyManagement>
        <dependencies>
            <dependency>
                <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
                <artifactId>spring-boot-dependencies</artifactId>
                <version>3.2.8</version>
                <type>pom</type>
                <scope>import</scope>
            </dependency>
        </dependencies>
    </dependencyManagement>

    <dependencies>
        <!-- Spring Boot core -->
        <dependency>
            <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
            <artifactId>spring-boot-starter</artifactId>
        </dependency>

        <!-- Web support (for REST endpoints) -->
        <dependency>
            <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
            <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-web</artifactId>
        </dependency>

        <!-- Jakarta EE APIs as provided -->
        <dependency>
            <groupId>jakarta.enterprise</groupId>
            <artifactId>jakarta.enterprise.cdi-api</artifactId>
            <scope>provided</scope>
        </dependency>
        <dependency>
            <groupId>jakarta.persistence</groupId>
            <artifactId>jakarta.persistence-api</artifactId>
            <scope>provided</scope>
        </dependency>
        <dependency>
            <groupId>jakarta.validation</groupId>
            <artifactId>jakarta.validation-api</artifactId>
            <scope>provided</scope>
        </dependency>
    </dependencies>

    <build>
        <plugins>
            <!-- Enables spring-boot:run and repackage -->
            <plugin>
                <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
                <artifactId>spring-boot-maven-plugin</artifactId>
            </plugin>
        </plugins>
    </build>

</project>

ChatGPT said:
The error you‚Äôre seeing:

‚Äòbuild.plugins.plugin.version‚Äô for org.springframework.boot:spring-boot-maven-plugin is missing
happens because when you don‚Äôt use spring-boot-starter-parent you must explicitly declare the version of the spring-boot-maven-plugin. The BOM you imported via <dependencyManagement> does not cover plugin versions.

Fix: Add the plugin <version> (3.2.8) to your POM
Replace your <build> section in kitchensink-util/pom.xml with this:

<build>
  <plugins>
    <!-- Enables spring-boot:run and repackaging -->
    <plugin>
      <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
      <artifactId>spring-boot-maven-plugin</artifactId>
      <version>3.2.8</version> <!-- <- explicit version required -->
    </plugin>
  </plugins>
</build>
So your full POM becomes:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<project xmlns="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0"
         xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
         xsi:schemaLocation="
           http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0
           http://maven.apache.org/xsd/maven-4.0.0.xsd">

  <modelVersion>4.0.0</modelVersion>

  <!-- Keep your multi-module parent -->
  <parent>
    <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
    <artifactId>kitchensink-parent</artifactId>
    <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
  </parent>

  <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>

  <properties>
    <java.version>21</java.version>
    <project.build.sourceEncoding>UTF-8</project.build.sourceEncoding>
  </properties>

  <!-- Import Spring Boot‚Äôs BOM for dependency versions -->
  <dependencyManagement>
    <dependencies>
      <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-dependencies</artifactId>
        <version>3.2.8</version>
        <type>pom</type>
        <scope>import</scope>
      </dependency>
    </dependencies>
  </dependencyManagement>

  <dependencies>
    <!-- Core Spring Boot -->
    <dependency>
      <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
      <artifactId>spring-boot-starter</artifactId>
    </dependency>
    <!-- Web support -->
    <dependency>
      <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
      <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-web</artifactId>
    </dependency>

    <!-- Jakarta APIs (provided by legacy container) -->
    <dependency>
      <groupId>jakarta.enterprise</groupId>
      <artifactId>jakarta.enterprise.cdi-api</artifactId>
      <scope>provided</scope>
    </dependency>
    <dependency>
      <groupId>jakarta.persistence</groupId>
      <artifactId>jakarta.persistence-api</artifactId>
      <scope>provided</scope>
    </dependency>
    <dependency>
      <groupId>jakarta.validation</groupId>
      <artifactId>jakarta.validation-api</artifactId>
      <scope>provided</scope>
    </dependency>
  </dependencies>

  <build>
    <plugins>
      <!-- Now with explicit version -->
      <plugin>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-maven-plugin</artifactId>
        <version>3.2.8</version>
      </plugin>
    </plugins>
  </build>
</project>

You‚Äôre right‚Äîyour util module only has the copied Resources.java. We still need to add the Spring Boot entry‚Äêpoint class so you can actually launch the service.

1. Create Application.java
In the Project pane, under

kitchensink-util
‚îî‚îÄ src/main/java
   ‚îî‚îÄ org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util

Application

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import org.springframework.boot.SpringApplication;
import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.SpringBootApplication;

@SpringBootApplication
public class Application {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SpringApplication.run(Application.class, args);
    }
}
2. Annotate your helper

import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;

@Component
public class Resources {
    // ... existing code ...
}

ChatGPT said:
Great‚Äînow that both Application.java and Resources.java live in your Spring-Boot module and you can run the app, let‚Äôs expose a simple REST endpoint to prove it all works.

Phase 3: Expose a REST Endpoint
1. Create a Controller
Right-click on the package

kitchensink-util
‚îî‚îÄ src/main/java/org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util
Choose New ‚Üí Java Class ‚Üí name it:

ResourceController
Paste in:

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
@RequestMapping("/api/resources")
public class ResourceController {

    private final Resources resources;

    public ResourceController(Resources resources) {
        this.resources = resources;
    }

    @GetMapping("/ping")
    public String ping() {
        // for demo, call any Resources method or just return a static string
        return "PONG from Resources: " + resources.toString();
    }
}
@RestController makes this a web endpoint.

@RequestMapping sets the base path.

@GetMapping("/ping") defines GET /api/resources/ping.

2. Rebuild & Run
In the Maven tool window, run kitchensink-util ‚Üí spring-boot:run (or Run ‚ÄòApplication.main()‚Äô).

Once you see ‚ÄúStarted Application‚Äù in the console, open your browser:

http://localhost:8080/api/resources/ping
You should get back something like:

PONG from Resources: org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util.Resources@5f184fc6
That gives you a fully functional slice:

Legacy module (kitchensink/**) untouched.

Modern module (kitchensink-util/**) running Spring Boot on Java 21.

A real HTTP endpoint wired to your old helper code.

Let me know how the ping endpoint behaves, and then we can discuss wiring more meaningful business logic (or replacing JPA calls with MongoDB, if you‚Äôre going for the stretch goal).

ChatGPT said:
Exactly‚Äînow that you‚Äôve pulled all of your helper code into kitchensink-util, you can lean your legacy WAR on that shared JAR instead of its own util package. Here‚Äôs how to wire it up:

1. Remove the old util folder from the legacy module
In Project view, expand:

2phase1
‚îî‚îÄ kitchensink/src/main/java/org/jboss/as/quickstarts/kitchensink
   ‚îî‚îÄ util
Right-click the entire util folder ‚Üí Delete.

(Optional) Delete any Javadoc or tests under src/main/resources or src/test/java that refer to it.

2. Add a compile-time dependency on your new module
Open kitchensink/pom.xml and under <dependencies> add:

<dependency>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
  <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
</dependency>
Note: Because both modules share the same parent, you don‚Äôt need to configure <scope>‚Äîcompile is the default.

3. Verify your parent POM modules
Make sure your kitchensink-parent/pom.xml lists them in the right order:

<modules>
  <module>kitchensink-util</module>    <!-- shared util must build first -->
  <module>kitchensink</module>         <!-- legacy WAR depends on util -->
</modules>
If it was reversed, swap those two lines so Maven builds kitchensink-util before kitchensink.

4. Update any import paths (if needed)
Because both modules use the same package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util, your legacy code shouldn‚Äôt need import changes. If you did rename packages in the helper, update imports in any legacy class that injected or referenced Resources.

5. Rebuild the multi-module project
In the top-level Maven tool window (pointing at kitchensink-parent), click Refresh (üîÑ).

Run the install lifecycle on the parent:

kitchensink-parent ‚Üí Lifecycle ‚Üí install
This will build & install kitchensink-util into your local repo, then build your WAR against it.

Confirm both modules build cleanly and that the WAR no longer contains its old util code but still compiles/injects Resources.

6. Redeploy your legacy WAR
Finally, redeploy your kitchensink WAR to JBoss as before. It‚Äôll now pick up your shared helper from the kitchensink-util JAR on the classpath.

That‚Äôs it‚Äîyou‚Äôve successfully phased out the embedded helper in the legacy app in favor of your new, Spring-Boot-ready shared module. Let me know if you hit any snags!

Your parent POM‚Äôs <modules> section needs two fixes:

<project xmlns="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0"
         xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
         xsi:schemaLocation="http://maven.apache.org/POM/4.0.0

You‚Äôve nailed it‚Äîyour legacy kitchensink module isn‚Äôt pulling in the JAR you just built, so it can‚Äôt see the org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util package anymore. Let‚Äôs fix that.

1. Add a dependency on kitchensink-util
Open kitchensink/pom.xml (the WAR‚Äôs POM) and inside the <dependencies> section add:

<dependency>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
  <!-- use the same version as your parent -->
  <version>${project.version}</version>
</dependency>
It should look roughly like:

<project ‚Ä¶>
  ‚Ä¶
  <parent> ‚Ä¶ </parent>
  <artifactId>kitchensink</artifactId>
  ‚Ä¶
  <dependencies>
    <!-- your new shared util module -->
    <dependency>
      <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
      <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
      <version>${project.version}</version>
    </dependency>

    <!-- all your other Jakarta EE provided dependencies -->
    <dependency>
      <groupId>jakarta.enterprise</groupId>
      <artifactId>jakarta.enterprise.cdi-api</artifactId>
      <scope>provided</scope>
    </dependency>
    <!-- etc‚Ä¶ -->
  </dependencies>
  ‚Ä¶
</project>
Because this module shares the parent‚Äôs <version>, you can use ${project.version} to keep it in sync.

2. Ensure correct module ordering
Make sure your parent POM has the modules in this order:

<modules>
  <module>kitchensink-util</module>
  <module>kitchensink</module>
</modules>
That way kitchensink-util builds first, installs its JAR into your reactor, and then kitchensink will pick it up.

3. Remove the old util folder
If you haven‚Äôt already, delete the legacy

kitchensink/src/main/java/org/jboss/as/quickstarts/kitchensink/util
directory so you don‚Äôt accidentally still have stale code there.

mvn clean install
You should now see:

kitchensink-util build and install successfully

kitchensink compile successfully against that new util JAR

Your Arquillian IT (MemberRegistrationIT.java) will now resolve org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util.Resources from the shared module.

Thought for 4 seconds
When you copy a .war straight into standalone/deployments by hand, the Management Console won‚Äôt automatically pick up that you‚Äôve ‚Äúmanaged‚Äù it via the UI‚Äîso the ‚ÄúDeployments‚Äù table stays empty even though Undertow is serving your app on :8080. 2) Drop the marker file
JBoss‚Äôs hot-deploy scanner looks for marker files:

Copy your WAR:

Then create the ‚Äú.dodeploy‚Äù flag next to it:

touch $EAP_HOME/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.war.dodeploy
After a few seconds the server will auto-deploy it, and the Console‚Äôs Deployments view will refresh to show:

Name	Runtime Name	Enabled	Last Update
kitchensink.war	kitchensink.war	‚úÖ	2025-05-08‚Ä¶
Verifying / Undeploying via CLI

$EAP_HOME/bin/jboss-cli.sh --connect

# list
deployment-info

# undeploy the old one

# redeploy the new one
deploy target/kitchensink.war
Once the WAR is properly managed by the server, you‚Äôll see it in the Console and be able to click its row to view status, URL mappings (so you know it‚Äôs the new one), enable/disable or undeploy without touching the filesystem again.

You said:
yes i do undersntd this but why then http://localhost:8080/kitchensink/index.jsf is reachable and running?
ChatGPT said:

Thought for 6 seconds
Because JBoss‚Äôs file-based auto-deployer picks up anything sitting in standalone/deployments (or any exploded .war/ there) at startup (or whenever you touch the .dodeploy marker), your old kitchensink.war is still being deployed into Undertow and served on port 8080‚Äîregardless of what the Management Console shows.

The Console‚Äôs Deployments page only lists deployments that it ‚Äúknows about‚Äù via the management API (i.e. ones you added through the GUI or via the CLI deploy command). Manually copying a WAR into the deployments folder bypasses the management API and uses the file-scanner instead, so it won‚Äôt appear in that table‚Äîyet the server is still running it.

How to prove it
List via CLI

$EAP_HOME/bin/jboss-cli.sh --connect --commands="deployment-info"
You‚Äôll see kitchensink.war in the ‚Äúauto-deployed‚Äù list.

Undeploy via CLI

undeploy kitchensink.war
Now hit http://localhost:8080/kitchensink/index.jsf ‚Üí you‚Äôll get a 404.

Re-deploy under management control

deploy target/kitchensink.war
That WAR will now show up in the Console‚Äôs Deployments tab, and you‚Äôll access the same JSF page at /kitchensink/index.jsf.

In short
Auto-deploy (file drop) ‚â† Managed deploy (API/CLI/GUI)
Manually dropped WARs run just fine, but won‚Äôt appear in the GUI‚Äôs deployment list until you add them via the management API (CLI or the ‚Äú‚ûï Add‚Äù button in the Console).

Thought for 6 seconds
Your standalone directory is in the parent of bin. From:

Why it still serves /kitchensink/index.jsf even though the Console shows no deployments
JBoss EAP, by default, has its deployment-scanner enabled in standalone.xml. That scanner watches the standalone/deployments folder and will hot-deploy anything you drop there (provided you include the proper .dodeploy marker or the scanner is configured for auto-deploy). These ‚Äúfile-based‚Äù deployments aren‚Äôt registered through the management API, so the Admin Console‚Äôs Deployments screen stays empty‚Äîbut Undertow is still serving the WAR.

How to see it in the Management Console

  --commands="deploy /full/path/to/kitchensink.war"
Once you do that, kitchensink.war will show up under Deployments ‚Üí Enabled in the Console.

How to undeploy your old file-drop WAR
If you want to get rid of the legacy, file-dropped version so you don‚Äôt accidentally hit the old code:

You can then redeploy under management control (CLI or Console) so that it does appear in the Admin Console and you‚Äôve got one single source of truth.

ChatGPT said:
You‚Äôre almost there ‚Äì you‚Äôve successfully split off all of your @Produces methods into the kitchensink-util JAR, but Weld (WildFly‚Äôs CDI) still can‚Äôt see them, so your legacy WAR can‚Äôt satisfy its @Inject EntityManager and @Inject Logger points. Let‚Äôs fix it in two quick steps:

1. Turn your util JAR into a proper CDI bean archive
Add a beans.xml so CDI will scan it.
Create

src/main/resources/META-INF/beans.xml
with these contents (even an empty file will do):

<beans xmlns="http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee"
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
       xsi:schemaLocation="
         http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee
         http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee/beans_2_0.xsd"
       bean-discovery-mode="annotated">
</beans>
Annotate your producer class with a CDI bean‚Äêdefining stereotype.

// replace your Spring @Component
// import jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped;
@ApplicationScoped
public class Resources {

    @Produces
    @PersistenceContext
    private EntityManager em;

    @Produces
    public Logger produceLog(InjectionPoint ip) {
        return Logger.getLogger(ip.getMember().getDeclaringClass().getName());
    }
}
Use jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped (or @Singleton) instead of Spring‚Äôs @Component.

Make sure your imports are jakarta. ones (jakarta.enterprise.inject.Produces, jakarta.persistence.PersistenceContext, etc.)

With that in place, Weld will discover your Resources bean, register both the EM‚Äêproducer and the Logger‚Äêproducer, and satisfy all of your legacy injections.

2. Add the util JAR as a real dependency of your WAR
Inside your kitchensink module‚Äôs pom.xml, under <dependencies> (not just in dependencyManagement), add:

<dependency>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
  <version>${project.version}</version>
  <!-- scope can be "compile" (default) so it's bundled into the WAR -->
</dependency>
Then rebuild:

cd /path/to/kitchensink-parent
mvn clean install -DskipTests
That gives you:

kitchensink-util-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar installed

kitchensink.war which now contains your util classes + beans.xml

Redeploy
Undeploy old ‚Äì remove any stray kitchensink.war* from standalone/deployments.

Deploy freshly built WAR, e.g. via the CLI:

jboss-cli.sh --connect \
  --command="deploy /path/to/kitchensink/target/kitchensink.war --force"
Verify in the Admin Console ‚Üí Deployments you now see exactly one enabled kitchensink.war.

Browse to

http://localhost:8080/kitchensink/index.jsf
and your app should come up without any injection errors.

That will give Weld a bean‚Äêarchive to scan (thanks to beans.xml and @ApplicationScoped) and actually pull in your util‚Äêprovided EntityManager and Logger producers. Let me know how it goes!

You said:
where all this? inte the kitechnsind-util or in the legacy?
ChatGPT said:
Everything I described lives in your kitchensink-util module, except the Maven <dependency> entry, which goes into the legacy kitchensink module.

In kitchensink-util

Add src/main/resources/META-INF/beans.xml

Change your Resources.java to use CDI (@ApplicationScoped, @Produces, @PersistenceContext, etc.) instead of Spring

In kitchensink (the WAR)

In its pom.xml under <dependencies>, add:

<dependency>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
  <version>${project.version}</version>
</dependency>
Rebuild (mvn clean install) so the WAR bundles your util JAR + beans.xml

Then redeploy the WAR and Weld will pick up the EntityManager and Logger producers from your util archive.

ChatGPT said:

Thought for 5 seconds
It turns out Weld never saw your producer class, so none of your @Produces methods ever got registered. You need to do two things:

1) Make your util JAR a bean archive
By default you set

<META-INF/beans.xml>
  <beans bean-discovery-mode="annotated" ‚Ä¶>
  </beans>
</beans>
That means Weld will only look at classes that have a bean-defining annotation (e.g. @ApplicationScoped, @Singleton, etc.). You had only put Spring‚Äôs @Component there, so Weld skipped it entirely.

Fix either:

a) Switch to bean-discovery-mode="all" so every class in the JAR is scanned:

<META-INF/beans.xml>
<beans xmlns="http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee"
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
       xsi:schemaLocation="
         http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee
         http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee/beans_2_0.xsd"
       bean-discovery-mode="all">
</beans>
b) Or give your Resources.java a real CDI annotation, for example:

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.Produces;
import jakarta.persistence.EntityManager;
import jakarta.persistence.PersistenceContext;
import java.util.logging.Logger;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.spi.InjectionPoint;

@ApplicationScoped    // <-- makes this class a CDI bean
public class Resources {

    @Produces
    @PersistenceContext
    private EntityManager em;

    @Produces
    public Logger produceLog(InjectionPoint ip) {
       return Logger.getLogger(ip.getMember().getDeclaringClass().getName());
    }
}
Either one of those changes will cause Weld to register both your EntityManager and your Logger producers.

2) Include the util JAR in your WAR
In your kitchensink module‚Äôs pom.xml you had only put the util under <dependencyManagement>. You still need a plain <dependency> so Maven actually packages it:

<dependencies>
  <!-- other deps‚Ä¶ -->

  <!-- THIS makes the JAR show up in WEB-INF/lib -->
  <dependency>
    <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
    <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
    <version>${project.version}</version>
  </dependency>
</dependencies>
Then:

cd kitchensink-util
mvn clean install              ‚Üê installs your util.jar into your local repo
cd ../kitchensink
mvn clean package -DskipTests  ‚Üê rebuild the WAR, util.jar will be woven in
Now when you drop the newly generated kitchensink.war into EAP, Weld will see:

a beans.xml in WEB-INF/lib/kitchensink-util.jar!/META-INF/beans.xml

your Resources class as a CDI bean

both @Produces methods available for injection

And all those ‚ÄúUnsatisfied dependencies for EntityManager/Logger‚Äù errors will go away.

Give that a shot and then redeploy your WAR. Let me know how it goes!

No problem‚Äîhere‚Äôs the minimal Java tweak you still need in your Resources.java so that Weld actually picks up your producers:

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped;    // ‚Üê add this
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.Produces;
import jakarta.persistence.EntityManager;
import jakarta.persistence.PersistenceContext;
import java.util.logging.Logger;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.spi.InjectionPoint;

@ApplicationScoped    // ‚Üê this makes Resources a CDI bean in ‚Äúannotated‚Äù mode
public class Resources {

    @Produces
    @PersistenceContext
    private EntityManager em;

    @Produces
    public Logger produceLog(InjectionPoint ip) {
       return Logger.getLogger(ip.getMember().getDeclaringClass().getName());
    }
}
Add @ApplicationScoped (or any bean-defining CDI annotation) to the class.

Leave your beans.xml set to bean-discovery-mode="annotated" (so only classes with CDI annotations get scanned).

Once you‚Äôve done that, rebuild & install the util JAR, re-package your WAR (with the <dependency> entry for kitchensink-util in your kitchensink pom.xml), and redeploy. Weld will now see your EntityManager and Logger producers and the deployment errors will disappear.

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import jakarta.enterprise.inject.Produces;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.spi.InjectionPoint;
import jakarta.persistence.EntityManager;
import jakarta.persistence.PersistenceContext;

import java.util.logging.Logger;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;

/**
 * This class uses CDI to alias Jakarta EE resources, such as the persistence context, to CDI beans
 *
 * <p>
 * Example injection on a managed bean field:
 * </p>
 *
 * <pre>
 * &#064;Inject
 * private EntityManager em;
 * </pre>
 */
@Component
public class Resources {
    @Produces
    @PersistenceContext
    private EntityManager em;

    @Produces
    public Logger produceLog(InjectionPoint injectionPoint) {
        return Logger.getLogger(injectionPoint.getMember().getDeclaringClass().getName());
    }

}
ChatGPT said:

Thought for 5 seconds
You‚Äôve nearly got it ‚Äî the only thing missing is a proper CDI bean‚Äêdefining annotation on your Resources class. Right now you‚Äôre using Spring‚Äôs @Component, but in a Jakarta EE/WildFly environment with bean-discovery-mode="annotated" that class will never get picked up as a producer.

Remove the Spring import and annotation.

Add a CDI bean scope (e.g. @ApplicationScoped).

Your Resources.java should end up looking like this:

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped;      // ‚Üê add this
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.Produces;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.spi.InjectionPoint;
import jakarta.persistence.EntityManager;
import jakarta.persistence.PersistenceContext;
import java.util.logging.Logger;

/**
 * This class uses CDI to alias Jakarta EE resources, such as
 * the persistence context, to CDI beans.
 */
@ApplicationScoped                                       // ‚Üê bean‚Äêdefining CDI annotation
public class Resources {

    @Produces
    @PersistenceContext
    private EntityManager em;

    @Produces
    public Logger produceLog(InjectionPoint injectionPoint) {
        return Logger.getLogger(
            injectionPoint.getMember()
                          .getDeclaringClass()
                          .getName()
        );
    }
}
Next steps
Rebuild & install your util module:

cd kitchensink-util
mvn clean install
Make sure your legacy kitchensink/pom.xml actually depends on the util JAR. Under <dependencies> you need:

<dependency>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
  <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
</dependency>
(If you only put it in <dependencyManagement> but never in <dependencies> then it won‚Äôt get packaged.)

Rebuild & deploy your legacy WAR, then start WildFly/EAP again.
The Weld errors about missing EntityManager and Logger producers will go away now that CDI sees your producers in the shared util JAR.

ChatGPT said:

Thought for 18 seconds
Let‚Äôs take a deep breath and untangle what‚Äôs tripping up Weld:

WELD-001408 Unsatisfied dependencies for type EntityManager
and
Unsatisfied dependencies for type Logger

Those come from your legacy WAR‚Äôs beans like MemberRepository and MemberRegistration trying to @Inject EntityManager em and @Inject Logger log, but Weld can‚Äôt find any producer for them‚Äîbecause your shared Resources class in kitchensink-util was never picked up as a CDI bean.

1. Fix your Resources.java so CDI actually sees it
In kitchensink-util, change:

// before
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;

@Component
public class Resources {
    // ...
}
to:

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped;      // ‚Üê CDI scope
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.Produces;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.spi.InjectionPoint;
import jakarta.persistence.EntityManager;
import jakarta.persistence.PersistenceContext;
import java.util.logging.Logger;

/**
 * A CDI bean that provides JEE resources (EntityManager & Logger)
 * to the rest of the app.
 */
@ApplicationScoped                                       // ‚Üê bean‚Äêdefining annotation
public class Resources {

    @Produces
    @PersistenceContext
    private EntityManager em;

    @Produces
    public Logger produceLog(InjectionPoint ip) {
        return Logger.getLogger(ip.getMember()
                                  .getDeclaringClass()
                                  .getName());
    }
}
Remove the Spring @Component import.

Add @ApplicationScoped (or @Dependent) so that CDI will scan and register your producers when bean-discovery-mode="annotated" is in play.

2. Make sure you have a beans.xml in the util JAR
You already showed:

kitchensink-util/
 ‚îî‚îÄ src/main/resources/META-INF/beans.xml
and inside it:

<beans xmlns="http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee"
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
       xsi:schemaLocation="
         http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee
         http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee/beans_2_0.xsd"
       bean-discovery-mode="annotated">
</beans>
That‚Äôs correct ‚Äî CDI will only look for classes with bean‚Äêdefining annotations (like @ApplicationScoped) in that JAR.

3. Rebuild & install the util module
cd kitchensink-util
mvn clean install
You should see a kitchensink-util-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar in your local repo.

4. Declare the util JAR as a real dependency in your WAR POM
Open kitchensink/pom.xml and under <dependencies>‚Ä¶</dependencies> add:

    <!-- our shared CDI producers -->
    <dependency>
      <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
      <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
      <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
      <scope>provided</scope>  <!-- if it‚Äôs only needed at compile/deploy time -->
    </dependency>
Important: Don‚Äôt just put it in <dependencyManagement> ‚Äî it must appear in <dependencies> so the WAR actually sees the producers at compile and package time.

5. Rebuild the entire multi-module project
From the parent directory:

mvn clean package
You should now get:

kitchensink-util.jar with your CDI producers (EntityManager, Logger).

kitchensink.war that includes that JAR on its classpath and can satisfy all the @Inject points.

6. Redeploy your WAR to EAP/WildFly
cp kitchensink/target/kitchensink.war $JBOSS_HOME/standalone/deployments/

(standalone.sh will auto‚Äìredeploy when it sees a changed WAR in the deployments/ folder.)

Now Weld will find:

EntityManager via your @Produces @PersistenceContext field, and

Logger via your @Produces Logger produceLog(...) method

and your legacy JSF+REST+EJB application will start without those CDI errors.

Why you saw the old app still running on :8080/kitchensink
Because your previous deploy never truly failed: EAP auto-deployed the old WAR (with the old producers) and kept it alive even when you copied over a broken one. Once you bring in the fixed WAR (with the util JAR properly wired), the console at http://localhost:9990 ‚Üí Deployments will show your new deployment as Enabled, and hitting http://localhost:8080/kitchensink/index.jsf will load your updated app.

Let me know once you‚Äôve applied the @ApplicationScoped change, reinstalled the util JAR, added the <dependency> in your WAR POM, and done a full mvn clean package. We‚Äôll verify the Weld startup logs together and make sure you‚Äôre back on track. You‚Äôve got this!

ChatGPT said:

Thought for 1m 6s
It turned out nothing was ‚Äúwrong‚Äù with WildFly or Maven ‚Äì it was our bean‚Äêdiscovery. We had:

Pulled all of our Jakarta producers (the @Produces ‚Äì EntityManager and Logger) into a separate JAR, but

Marked that JAR‚Äôs class with Spring‚Äôs @Component instead of a CDI scope, and

Never actually declared the util-module as a real dependency of our WAR.

Because of that:

CDI never picked up your Resources class (so it never registered your @Produces EntityManager or @Produces Logger), and

the WAR never pulled in the util JAR at runtime, so when Weld went looking for a default EntityManager or a default Logger producer you got ‚Äúunsatisfied dependency‚Äù everywhere.

1) Fix your Resources.java
In kitchensink-util/src/main/java/.../Resources.java:

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.Produces;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.spi.InjectionPoint;
import jakarta.persistence.EntityManager;
import jakarta.persistence.PersistenceContext;
import java.util.logging.Logger;

/**
 * CDI bean‚Äêdefining annotation so Weld actually scans this class
 */
@ApplicationScoped
public class Resources {

    /** now the container will inject a proper EM into any @Inject EntityManager */
    @Produces
    @PersistenceContext
    private EntityManager em;

    /** and this will satisfy all your @Inject Logger log; points */
    @Produces
    public Logger produceLog(InjectionPoint ip) {
        return Logger.getLogger(ip.getMember().getDeclaringClass().getName());
    }

}
Replace import org.springframework.stereotype.Component; @Component
with
import jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped; @ApplicationScoped.

2) Make sure the util JAR actually gets pulled into your WAR
In your kitchensink/pom.xml, under <dependencies> (not just in <dependencyManagement>), add:

<dependency>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
  <version>1.0-SNAPSHOT</version>
</dependency>
This will ensure Maven packages kitchensink-util-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar inside your WAR‚Äôs WEB-INF/lib.

3) Verify you have a beans.xml for CDI
You already have it in your util module:

kitchensink-util
‚îî‚îÄ src
   ‚îî‚îÄ main
      ‚îî‚îÄ resources
         ‚îî‚îÄ META-INF
            ‚îî‚îÄ beans.xml  ‚Üê with bean-discovery-mode="annotated"
Optionally, if you want CDI to see everything at the WAR level, you can also put a WEB-INF/beans.xml into your kitchensink module.

4) Rebuild & redeploy
From the root of your multi-module project:

mvn clean install
Then copy the newly built WAR over and start EAP:

cp kitchensink/target/kitchensink.war ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/
~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/bin/standalone.sh
Now Weld will see your @Produces methods (because Resources is truly a CDI bean) and supply both the EntityManager and the Logger, so those ‚Äúunsatisfied dependencies‚Äù will go away and your app will start cleanly.

Let me know if you hit anything else!

The reason you‚Äôre still getting unsatisfied‚Äêdependency errors in your legacy WAR is that your new kitchensink-util module (with your CDI @Produces methods for EntityManager and Logger) never actually ends up on the WAR‚Äôs classpath. 1) Add the util JAR as a dependency in the WAR

        <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
        <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
        <!-- version is inherited from the parent POM -->
    </dependency>
So your WAR POM will look something like this (only the relevant bits shown):

    <!-- <<< add this block: >>> -->

      <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>

    <!-- your other Jakarta-EE APIs, Hibernate, Arquillian, etc. -->

      <scope>provided</scope>
    </dependency>
    ‚Ä¶
  </dependencies>
</project>

At the top level (the parent), run:

mvn clean install
This will build kitchensink-util first, then kitchensink, installing both into your local repo.

Package and deploy your WAR:

(Or manually copy target/kitchensink.war into $EAP_HOME/standalone/deployments.)

In your WAR‚Äôs exploded or .war under WEB-INF/lib/, you should now see kitchensink-util-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar.

ChatGPT said:

Thought for 18 seconds
Your WAR POM is actually correct now‚Äîthe snippet you pasted does pull in kitchensink-util.jar at compile‚Äêtime:

<dependency>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
  <version>${project.version}</version>
</dependency>
So the fact that Weld is still complaining about missing EntityManager and Logger producers means one of two things:

1. Your util JAR never made it into the WAR
Rebuild & inspect
From the top‚Äêlevel folder run:

mvn clean install
Then:

jar tf kitchensink/target/kitchensink.war | grep kitchensink-util
You should see something like:

WEB-INF/lib/kitchensink-util-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar
If you don‚Äôt, you‚Äôre still deploying the old exploded WAR (or forgot to mvn install the util).

Clean out the old deployment
In $EAP_HOME/standalone/deployments delete all kitchensink files (kitchensink.war, kitchensink.war.deployed, kitchensink.war.failed), then copy the newly built target/kitchensink.war back in and let it redeploy.

2. CDI isn‚Äôt discovering your producers class
Even if the JAR is there, Weld will only scan a bean archive if it both:

Contains a META-INF/beans.xml

Has bean-defining annotations (or producer methods/fields)

You showed that your util module has:

kitchensink-util
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ src
    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ main
        ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ java/org/jboss/as/quickstarts/kitchensink/util/Resources.java
        ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ resources/META-INF/beans.xml
But your Resources.java is annotated with Spring‚Äôs @Component:

import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;

@Component
public class Resources {
  @Produces @PersistenceContext
  private EntityManager em;

  @Produces
  public Logger produceLog(InjectionPoint ip) { ‚Ä¶ }
}
Weld will ignore Spring‚Äôs @Component. You must use a CDI scope annotation (or nothing, relying on the presence of @Produces to make it a bean) and remove the Spring import. For example:

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.Produces;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.spi.InjectionPoint;
import jakarta.persistence.EntityManager;
import jakarta.persistence.PersistenceContext;
import java.util.logging.Logger;

@ApplicationScoped
public class Resources {
    @Produces
    @PersistenceContext
    private EntityManager em;

    @Produces
    public Logger produceLog(InjectionPoint ip) {
        return Logger.getLogger(ip.getMember().getDeclaringClass().getName());
    }
}
Replace @Component with @ApplicationScoped (or any CDI scope).

Remove import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;.

TL;DR
Verify kitchensink-util.jar is really in your WAR‚Äôs WEB-INF/lib.

Clean old deployments, redeploy the freshly built WAR.

Change your Resources.java to use a CDI scope (@ApplicationScoped) instead of Spring‚Äôs @Component, rebuild, reinstall, redeploy.

Once those two things are in place, Weld will pick up your @Produces EntityManager and @Produces Logger and the unsatisfied‚Äêdependency errors will go away.

ChatGPT said:
The ‚ÄúDuplicateServiceException‚Äù is coming from the fact that your Kitchensink quickstart still ships its own *-ds.xml file defining the java:jboss/datasources/KitchensinkQuickstartDS data-source, and WildFly/EAP is detecting and deploying that DS in two places:

Once from the legacy quickstart‚Äôs WEB-INF/kitchensink-ds.xml (or similar) inside your WAR,

And again from the file‚Äêdrop DS definition in standalone/deployments.

You end up with two services both trying to register the same JNDI data‚Äêsource, so the second one blows up.

A) Quick fix: remove the stray DS definition
On the server

cd ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments
# remove any DS file for kitchensink
rm kitchensink*ds.xml*
# also remove any failed markers
rm kitchensink*.war.failed
In your WAR
If you still need the KitchensinkQuickstartDS, let WildFly manage one copy. The easiest is to strip it out of your WAR so it‚Äôs only defined once:

In your kitchensink module, run:

rm src/main/webapp/WEB-INF/kitchensink-ds.xml
(and any other *-ds.xml you find under src/main/webapp/WEB-INF)

Rebuild & redeploy

mvn clean package
cp kitchensink/target/kitchensink-1.0-SNAPSHOT.war \
   ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.war
touch ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.war.dodeploy
tail -F ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/log/server.log
You should now see only a single ‚ÄúStarting deployment of "kitchensink.war"‚Äù ‚Üí ‚ÄúDeployed "kitchensink.war‚Äù and no more DS duplicate errors.

B) Permanent solution: exclude the DS from your WAR‚Äôs packaging
If you‚Äôd rather keep the DS file in source but prevent it from ending up in the WAR, add this to your kitchensink/pom.xml:

<build>
  <plugins>
    <plugin>
      <artifactId>maven-war-plugin</artifactId>
      <version>3.3.2</version>
      <configuration>
        <!-- exclude any DS descriptor so you only get the one in deployments/ -->
        <packagingExcludes>WEB-INF/*-ds.xml</packagingExcludes>
      </configuration>
    </plugin>
  </plugins>
</build>
Then:

mvn clean package
will produce a WAR that no longer contains kitchensink-ds.xml, so WildFly will deploy the DS from standalone/deployments only once.

After either of these, you‚Äôll have a single, correctly deployed KitchensinkQuickstartDS, and your WAR will drop in without the ‚ÄúDuplicateServiceException.‚Äù Once that‚Äôs cleared, Weld will boot cleanly and your modernized util module will back your legacy code as intended.

Thought for 11 seconds
The stack-trace tells us Weld is choking on jakarta.servlet.http.HttpServlet$NoBodyAsyncContextListener because two different copies of the Servlet API are ending up in the same classloader, and their InnerClasses attributes don‚Äôt match.

That almost always means your WAR has bundled a Servlet API JAR it shouldn‚Äôt. The quickstart‚Äôs WAR must not include any jakarta.servlet-api.jar (or old javax.servlet-api.jar)‚ÄîWildFly/EAP already provides it.

1) Verify what‚Äôs in your WAR
Run this in your kitchensink module:

jar tf target/kitchensink-1.0-SNAPSHOT.war | grep servlet-api
You should see nothing. If you do see something like:

WEB-INF/lib/jakarta.servlet-api-5.0.0.jar
then that is the culprit.

2) Exclude the Servlet API from your WAR
A) If you have an explicit dependency on jakarta.servlet-api
In your kitchensink/pom.xml, either remove it completely or mark it as provided:

<dependency>
  <groupId>jakarta.servlet</groupId>
  <artifactId>jakarta.servlet-api</artifactId>
  <scope>provided</scope>
</dependency>
B) If it‚Äôs coming in transitively
Find which dependency is dragging it in:

mvn dependency:tree -Dincludes=jakarta.servlet:jakarta.servlet-api
Then add an <exclusion> under that dependency:

<dependency>
  <groupId>some.group</groupId>
  <artifactId>some-artifact-that-brings-in-servlet-api</artifactId>
  <exclusions>
    <exclusion>
      <groupId>jakarta.servlet</groupId>
      <artifactId>jakarta.servlet-api</artifactId>
    </exclusion>
  </exclusions>
</dependency>
3) Rebuild & Redeploy
# from your project root
mvn clean package

# clean out the old deployments
rm ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.*

# copy in the fresh WAR
cp kitchensink/target/kitchensink-1.0-SNAPSHOT.war \
   ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.war

# trigger a deploy
touch ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.war.dodeploy

# watch the server logs
tail -F ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/log/server.log
You should now see a clean deployment (no DuplicateService or IncompatibleClassChangeError).

Let me know what jar tf ‚Ä¶ | grep servlet-api shows, and we‚Äôll nail down exactly which dependency line to fix.

Thought for 50 seconds
Let‚Äôs tackle the two fatal problems in one go:

Your CDI producers in kitchensink-util never actually become CDI beans, so Weld never sees your @Produces EntityManager and @Produces Logger ‚Äì hence the ‚ÄúUnsatisfied dependencies‚Äù on EntityManager and Logger.

Weld is scanning every class under jakarta.servlet‚Ä¶ in your WAR (including container‚Äêprovided ones) and choking on the servlet API mismatch ‚Äì hence the IncompatibleClassChangeError on HttpServlet$NoBodyAsyncContextListener.

1) Turn your util JAR into a proper CDI bean archive
In kitchensink-util:

Remove the Spring annotation. Open
src/main/java/org/jboss/as/quickstarts/kitchensink/util/Resources.java
and:

- import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;
@Component
public class Resources {
becomes

- import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;
+ import jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped;
@ApplicationScoped
public class Resources {
Add a beans.xml so CDI will actually pick up your producer class.
Create
src/main/resources/META-INF/beans.xml
with:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<beans xmlns="http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee"
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
       xsi:schemaLocation="http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee
                           http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee/beans_2_0.xsd"
       bean-discovery-mode="annotated"
       version="2.0"/>
This turns your JAR into a CDI bean archive and only scans classes with bean-defining annotations (your @ApplicationScoped Resources).

Re-install the util JAR:

cd kitchensink-util
mvn clean install
2) Prevent Weld from scanning all servlet classes in your WAR
In your kitchensink WAR module:

Add a WEB-INF/beans.xml that tells Weld to only pick up annotated beans (so it won‚Äôt even look at jakarta.servlet.*):

Create or edit
src/main/webapp/WEB-INF/beans.xml
to:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<beans xmlns="http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee"
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
       xsi:schemaLocation="http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee
                           http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee/beans_2_0.xsd"
       bean-discovery-mode="annotated"
       version="2.0"/>
Clean up duplicate API deps. In your WAR POM remove any repeated ${jakarta.enterprise.cdi-api}, ${jakarta.persistence-api}, etc. ‚Äî you only need them once, and in provided scope. Having them declared twice can confuse Maven‚Äôs effective model.

Re-package the WAR:

cd ../kitchensink
mvn clean package
3) Redeploy to EAP
Remove every old artifact and any leftover *.dodeploy or *.failed files:

rm ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink*.*
Copy the fresh WAR:

cp target/kitchensink-1.0-SNAPSHOT.war \
   ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.war
touch ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.war.dodeploy
Watch the log:

tail -F ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/log/server.log
You should now see:

No more ‚ÄúUnsatisfied dependencies for EntityManager‚Äù (your producer is picked up).

No more servlet‚ÄêAPI mismatch errors (Weld won‚Äôt scan container classes).

Your app should come up cleanly.

Give that a shot and let me know if any of those errors persist!

‚Äî

mvn clean package
2) Make sure you haven‚Äôt packaged the Servlet API
Your WAR must not include jakarta.servlet-api.jar in WEB-INF/lib. That should always be <scope>provided</scope>. Let‚Äôs check:

jar tf target/kitchensink-1.0-SNAPSHOT.war | grep servlet-api
If you see anything like WEB-INF/lib/jakarta.servlet-api-*.jar, remove it by editing your POM:

- <dependency>
-   <groupId>jakarta.servlet</groupId>
-   <artifactId>jakarta.servlet-api</artifactId>
-   <!-- NO version and NO default scope -->
- </dependency>
+ <!-- remove any servlet-api dependency entirely; the container provides it -->
Then re-build again:

mvn clean package
Redeploy
Clean out all kitchensink*.war* from $EAP_HOME/standalone/deployments.

Copy in the fresh WAR:

cp target/kitchensink-1.0-SNAPSHOT.war \
   ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.war

Watch the server log:

tail -F ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/log/server.log
With a proper beans.xml and no servlet-api jar in your WAR, Weld will only scan your application beans and your @Produces methods for EntityManager and Logger, and will not attempt to re-scan the container‚Äôs HttpServlet classes. Let me know what you see after those two checks!

Thought for 22 seconds
That error

IncompatibleClassChangeError: jakarta.servlet.http.HttpServlet and jakarta.servlet.http.HttpServlet$NoBodyAsyncContextListener disagree on InnerClasses attribute
almost always means you‚Äôre accidentally bundling a second copy of the servlet API (or a servlet implementation) inside your WAR, so Weld tries to instrument the container‚Äôs HttpServlet class but finds a mismatched InnerClasses entry.

Even though you didn‚Äôt see a standalone jakarta.servlet-api.jar in WEB-INF/lib, you did pull in Spring-Boot Starter Web (and its embedded Tomcat) into your kitchensink-util JAR, which then got dropped into your WAR. Tomcat-embed-core itself contains its own jakarta.servlet.http.HttpServlet class, and that collides with JBoss EAP‚Äôs.

What to do:

Verify the clash
In your kitchensink folder, run:

jar tf target/kitchensink-1.0-SNAPSHOT.war \
  | grep -E 'WEB-INF/lib/.*(tomcat|servlet).*\.jar'
jar tf target/kitchensink-1.0-SNAPSHOT.war \
  | grep HttpServlet.class
If you see e.g. WEB-INF/lib/tomcat-embed-core-*.jar (or anything that contains jakarta/servlet/http/HttpServlet.class), that‚Äôs your culprit.

Strip out Spring-Boot from the EAP deployment
Unless you really intend to run a Spring-Boot application inside JBoss EAP (which is un¬≠usual), remove these two lines from kitchensink-util/pom.xml:

- <!-- Core Spring Boot -->
- <dependency>
-   <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
-   <artifactId>spring-boot-starter</artifactId>
- </dependency>
- <!-- Web support (pulls in Tomcat Embed!) -->
- <dependency>
-   <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
-   <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-web</artifactId>
- </dependency>
Optionally you can mark them <scope>provided</scope> if you truly need Spring in the WAR‚Äîbut the safest is to remove them entirely so no embedded servlet impl ships into WEB-INF/lib.

Rebuild & redeploy clean

cd kitchensink
mvn clean package
rm ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink*.war*
cp target/kitchensink-1.0-SNAPSHOT.war \
   ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.war
touch ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/deployments/kitchensink.war.dodeploy
tail -F ~/jboss/jboss-eap-8.0/standalone/log/server.log
Double-check your beans.xml
Make sure you have exactly one src/main/webapp/WEB-INF/beans.xml so Weld only scans your beans:

jar tf target/kitchensink-1.0-SNAPSHOT.war | grep WEB-INF/beans.xml
If it‚Äôs missing, create it:

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<beans xmlns="http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee"
       xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
       xsi:schemaLocation="http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee
                           http://xmlns.jcp.org/xml/ns/javaee/beans_2_0.xsd"
       bean-discovery-mode="annotated"
       version="2.0"/>
Once there are no embedded servlet classes in your WAR and your beans.xml is present, JBoss Weld will stop trying to instrument HttpServlet in the container, and your CDI producers for EntityManager and Logger will be picked up normally. Let me know how it looks after those changes!

ChatGPT said:

Thought for 18 seconds
The WAR you‚Äôre deploying still contains embedded Tomcat (Spring Boot‚Äôs default) which is colliding with the servlet APIs in WildFly/EAP. You need to stop packaging those JARs into your legacy kitchensink.war. You can do that one of two ways:

1) Mark Spring-Boot dependencies in kitchensink-util as provided
In kitchensink-util/pom.xml, change your Spring-Boot deps to:

<dependencies>
  <!-- don‚Äôt ship the container‚Ä¶ -->
  <dependency>
    <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
    <artifactId>spring-boot-starter</artifactId>
    <scope>provided</scope>
  </dependency>
  <dependency>
    <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
    <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-web</artifactId>
    <scope>provided</scope>
  </dependency>
  <!-- your Jakarta APIs, etc‚Ä¶ -->
</dependencies>
This way you can still compile against Spring Boot locally, but Maven won‚Äôt package Tomcat into your util JAR (and transitively into the WAR).

2) Exclude Spring-Boot from the legacy WAR‚Äôs dependency on kitchensink-util
In kitchensink/pom.xml, update the kitchensink-util dependency to exclude the entire Spring-Boot stack:

<dependency>
  <groupId>com.example.kitchensink</groupId>
  <artifactId>kitchensink-util</artifactId>
  <version>${project.version}</version>
  <exclusions>
    <!-- Prevent pulling in Spring Boot + embedded Tomcat -->
    <exclusion>
      <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
      <artifactId>spring-boot-starter</artifactId>
    </exclusion>
    <exclusion>
      <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
      <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-web</artifactId>
    </exclusion>

Thought for 11 seconds
That Maven error isn‚Äôt coming from your exclusions at all but from the fact that the WAR plugin can‚Äôt find a web.xml and is by default running in ‚Äúupdate‚Äù mode, which requires either:

A <webXml> element in your POM, or

An existing /WEB-INF/web.xml on disk to merge against.

Your kitchensink quickstart originally shipped its own src/main/webapp/WEB-INF/web.xml. If you removed or renamed that, Maven will abort with exactly the message you‚Äôre seeing.

You have two choices:

A) Put the original WEB-INF/web.xml back
Make sure that

kitchensink/src/main/webapp/WEB-INF/web.xml
exists and contains the JSF/Faces servlet mapping that the quickstart needs. Then the WAR plugin will pick it up automatically and your exclusions will work just fine.

B) Tell the WAR plugin to not require a web.xml
If you‚Äôre on Servlet‚Äâ3+ and you‚Äôre only using annotations you can disable the check. In your kitchensink/pom.xml, add:

<build>
  <plugins>
    <plugin>
      <groupId>org.apache.maven.plugins</groupId>
      <artifactId>maven-war-plugin</artifactId>
      <version>3.4.0</version>
      <configuration>
        <!-- allow no WEB-INF/web.xml -->
        <failOnMissingWebXml>false</failOnMissingWebXml>
      </configuration>
    </plugin>
  </plugins>
</build>
With that in place you can:

Restore your <dependency> on kitchensink-util with the <exclusions> we gave you earlier (to strip out Tomcat).

Run mvn clean package again ‚Äî you should now get a .war without any Spring-Boot/Tomcat JARs inside.

Drop that WAR into EAP‚Äôs standalone/deployments and you‚Äôll finally get a clean Weld/JPA startup.

Let me know which route you‚Äôd like to take (restore the original web.xml or go annotation-only), and I can help you stitch it in.

ChatGPT said:
This new error is telling you exactly what‚Äôs wrong ‚Äì your persistence unit is looking for a JNDI datasource called

java:jboss/datasources/KitchensinkQuickstartDS
but you haven‚Äôt defined one in your server, so Weld can‚Äôt wire up your EntityManager.

You have two easy options:

1) Deploy the Quickstart‚Äôs built-in DS descriptor
The original kitchensink quickstart comes with a file named kitchensink-ds.xml (usually under src/main/resources) that defines exactly this H2 datasource. Simply copy it into your EAP deployments folder alongside your WAR:

cp path/to/kitchensink-util/src/main/resources/kitchensink-ds.xml \
   $JBOSS_HOME/standalone/deployments/
You should see in the admin console under Deployments:

kitchensink-ds.xml (status ‚ÄúOK‚Äù)

kitchensink.war (status ‚ÄúOK‚Äù)

The server will pick up kitchensink-ds.xml on startup and register the DS at java:jboss/datasources/KitchensinkQuickstartDS.

2) Manually add the datasource via CLI or standalone.xml
Via the CLI
Start your server, then in a separate shell:

$JBOSS_HOME/bin/jboss-cli.sh --connect \
  '/subsystem=datasources/data-source=KitchensinkQuickstartDS:add('\
'jndi-name="java:jboss/datasources/KitchensinkQuickstartDS",'\
'driver-name="h2",'\
'connection-url="jdbc:h2:mem:test;DB_CLOSE_DELAY=-1;DB_CLOSE_ON_EXIT=FALSE",'\
'user-name="sa",password="sa")'
(If you haven‚Äôt already installed the H2 driver, you can do it in the same way, or use the built-in h2 that ships with EAP.)

In standalone.xml
Under <subsystem xmlns="urn:jboss:domain:datasources:...">, add:

<datasources>
  <datasource jndi-name="java:jboss/datasources/KitchensinkQuickstartDS"
              pool-name="KitchensinkQuickstartDS" enabled="true" use-java-context="true">
    <connection-url>jdbc:h2:mem:test;DB_CLOSE_DELAY=-1;DB_CLOSE_ON_EXIT=FALSE</connection-url>
    <driver>h2</driver>
    <security>
      <user-name>sa</user-name>
      <password>sa</password>
    </security>
  </datasource>
  <drivers>
    <driver name="h2" module="com.h2database.h2">
      <xa-datasource-class>org.h2.jdbcx.JdbcDataSource</xa-datasource-class>
    </driver>
  </drivers>
</datasources>
Once you‚Äôve got KitchensinkQuickstartDS registered, redeploy your WAR and the JPA injection errors will go away. Let me know which approach you‚Äôd like, or if you hit any snags!

package org.jboss.as.quickstarts.kitchensink.util;

import jakarta.enterprise.context.ApplicationScoped;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.Produces;
import jakarta.enterprise.inject.spi.InjectionPoint;
import jakarta.persistence.EntityManager;
import jakarta.persistence.PersistenceContext;
import java.util.logging.Logger;

/**
 * This class uses CDI to alias Jakarta EE resources, such as
 * the persistence context, to CDI beans.
 */
@ApplicationScoped                                       // ‚Üê bean‚Äêdefining CDI annotation
public class Resources {

    @Produces
    @PersistenceContext
    private EntityManager em;

    @Produces
    public Logger produceLog(InjectionPoint injectionPoint) {
        return Logger.getLogger(
                injectionPoint.getMember()
                        .getDeclaringClass()
                        .getName()
        );
    }
}
